  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/5617430-kristine"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1329869500i/5617430._UX100_CR0,8,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/5617430-kristine">Kristine</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">"should be?" No, MUST BE. Stephen King explains this better than I could in his book _On writing,_ but I find it to be true over and over again: I lea<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">"should be?" No, MUST BE. Stephen King explains this better than I could in his book _On writing,_ but I find it to be true over and over again: I learn to write by reading. I don't read anything that I think is really bad, but I learn from reading things I think are not very good by making myself put my finger on what isn't very good about it. I'm currently reading a novel by one of my very favorite authors and really NOT loving it, despite the fact that there's much she does really well as always. After a lot of thought I realized the problem - for me at least - is there's not enough plot. I'm all for character-driven stories, I don't need fast-paced action-packed ... whatever, but there's almost no forward motion in this one. The characters are really complicated people but mostly all they do is get older. I expected so much more from her - <br /><br />Wow, I could go on for another hour. Probably should fix dinner instead ...<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

  <span id="freeText14821648601047428834" style="display:none">Read on Scribd!<br /><br />When Liliana's Mum is shot dead on the streets of Chicago, she finds herself being sent to her father in a different country, where she is forced to work as a servant. If she does a task wrong or fails to get back on time, she is punished. When she meets a guy, she finds herself having feelings for him. Truth is, Liliana doesn't know just how manipulative and shady he can be. This was a fast-paced read, very dialogue driven. I really wanted to get to know the characters more, since there was a little character connection for me. The ending did feel rushed and there are T/Ws for assault, violence so do bare that in mind before picking up this story. Sadly, the series wasn't for me and I won't be continuing on! </span>

I read it on one sitting.<br/><br/>Liliana is just a 13 year old typical teen when her American mother is murdered in front of her. With no other relatives--save for one aunt who has 6 children of her own and lives in poverty, she is forced to go to Columbia and live with a father she hasn't seen since she was 3 years old. <br/><br/>The character building and world bui</span>
  <span id="freeText17239754737200158087" style="display:none">I'm still not sure what genre it fits, but the book is outstanding. The author's voice is perfect for this story. And I could not put the book down. I read it on one sitting.<br /><br />Liliana is just a 13 year old typical teen when her American mother is murdered in front of her. With no other relatives--save for one aunt who has 6 children of her own and lives in poverty, she is forced to go to Columbia and live with a father she hasn't seen since she was 3 years old. <br /><br />The character building and world building are excellent. My heart broke for Liliana when her life came crashing down around her. I rooted for her. I was happy for her when she finally found a friend in her new employer. I despised her father. The cast of supporting characters all elicited emotional responses from me. <br /><br />It's first in a series and I look forward to reading more.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qafyBAlseelRwzcG/ZcexzU7nRLcCPK+WAOCjMqvNAir9szTt4rm9u62vIM1LuyUCb0+E95Z7arpqVlR50qj+w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TbPnTPz6J/mIFA7LG5gGywNOz5FZn6AVJQdt2RHC4rlP4tmbQhy45jdhhU7TIfSYP8hskFvOvwGUrbYEPCd1Sg==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer12497540345265102014">Neva Squires-Rodriguez was born and raised in a neighborhood located on the North Side of Chicago. Mother, Wife, Expert at multitasking, when she’s not writing newspaper columns or finishing up her latest novel, she is dispatching calls for her city’s 911 center.   <span id="freeText12497540345265102014" style="display:none">Neva Squires-Rodriguez was born and raised in a neighborhood located on the North Side of Chicago. Mother, Wife, Expert at multitasking, when she’s not writing newspaper columns or finishing up her latest novel, she is dispatching calls for her city’s 911 center. Perhaps this is what helps Neva create electrifying stories with a twist. <br /><br />Neva Squires-Rodriguez earned her Bachelor’s Degree from American Military University (APUS/AMU) and her Master’s Degree from National University, a feat which she worked very hard to obtain and says she will work even harder to pay off. <br /><br />She claims to be a typical American, full of dreams that will hopefully get her to a more comfortable lifestyle one day. She says, "God has a plan and I will follow wherever it is that He takes me."<br /><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.nevasquiresrodriguez.com">www.nevasquiresrodriguez.com</a><br /></span>
